## 1 ONA CLASS (PATROL CRAFT) (WPB)

ONA (ex-Pudú) LSG 1625

Displacement, tonnes: 110 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $26.6\times6.0\times2.0$  (87.3  $\times$  19.7  $\times$  6.6)

Speed, knots: 12

Range, n miles: 1,430 at 10 kt

Complement: 8 (2 officers)
Machinery: 2 Caterpillar 3412 12V diesels; 1,070 hp (798 kW); 2 shafts

Radars: Navigation: I-band

Comment: Built by ASENAV, Valdivia, in 1992 and operated as a pilot vessel by Ultratug until transferred to the Chilean Navy on 5 July 2011. The roles of the ship include surveillance, environmental monitoring and SAR. Based at Punta Arenas.

#### 4 GRUMETE DIAZ (DABUR) CLASS (COASTAL PATROL CRAFT) (WPB)

DIAZ LPC 1814 SALINAS LPC 1816 MACHADO LPC 1820 HUDSON LPC 1823

Displacement, tonnes: 34.5 standard: 40 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $19.8\times5.5\times1.8$  ( $65.0\times18.0\times5.9$ ) Speed, knots: 20

Range, n miles: 450 at 13 kt

Complement: 8 (2 officers)
Machinery: 2 diesels; 1,100 hp (820 kW) sustained; 2 shafts
Guns: 2 Oerlikon MK-IV 20/63 mm or 2—12.7 mm MGs.
Radars: Surface search: Racal Decca Super 101 Mk 3; I-band.

Comment: All have LPC numbers and Grumete precedes the ships' names. First six transferred from Israel and commissioned 3 January 1991. Second batch of four more transferred and commissioned 17 March 1995. A RIB inspection boat is carried on the stern. All underwent life extension refits in 2001–02 at Valparaiso and Puerto Montt. Two craft deleted in 2006, one in 2012, and three in 2013. Four craft refitted 2011-12 to extend life.

## 26 ARCHANGEL CLASS (RESPONSE BOATS) (WPBF)

LPM 4400-4413

LSR 4420-4431

Displacement, tonnes: 13.65 standard

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $13.5 \times 4.3 \times 0.91$  (44.3 × 14.1 × 3.0) Speed, knots: 37. Range, n miles: 300 at 25 kt

Complement: 3

Machinery: 2 Caterpillar C9 diesels; 1,100 hp (818 kW); 2 Hamilton 322 waterjets Guns: 1-7.62 mm MG.

Radars: Navigation: Furuno; I-band.

Comment: High-speed inshore patrol craft of aluminium construction and foam collar built by SAFE Boats International, Port Orchard, Washington. There had been 23 delivered by late 2013 and a further three by mid-2014. LSR series are self-righting and feature orange collar.

opeed, knots: 48

Radars: Navigation: Furuno 1834; I-band.

Comment: High-speed inshore patrol craft of aluminium construction and foam collar built by SAFE Boats International, Port Orchard, Washington. Full cabin version. Further 15 ordered in December 2017 under Rhin II Lacustre project to replace the Rodman 890 type craft used for riverine and lake patrol tasks. First batch of five delivered in December 2018 for final outfitting at ASMAR. Next five completed at ASMAR by April 2020, and the final five in November 2020.

# China

# PEOPLE'S LIBERATION ARMY NAVY (PLAN)

![](_page_1_Picture_4.jpeg)

#### Country overview

The People's Republic of China, proclaimed on 1 October 1949, is the world's third-largest country by area (3,695,000 square miles). It is bordered to the northwest by Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan, to the north by Mongolia, and Russia, to the south by Vietnam, Laos, Myanmar, India, Bhutan, and Nepal, to the east by North Korea and to the west by Pakistan, Afghanistan, and Tajikistan. It has a 7,830 n mile coastline with the Yellow, East China, and South China seas. There are more than 3,400 offshore islands of which Hainan is the largest. Sovereignty over Taiwan is also claimed. In the South China Sea there are territorial disputes between China, Brunei, Taiwan, Vietnam, Malaysia, Indonesia, and the Philippines and in the East China Sea between China, Japan, and South and in the East Chillad Sea Between Chillad, Japan, and Joun Korea. The principal ports are Shanghai, Qingdao, Shantou, Xiamen, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Hong Kong, Dalian, and Ningbo-Zhoushan. Overall there are 54,000 n miles of navigable inland waterways including the Yangtze River on which the port of Wuhan is situated. Territorial seas (12 n miles) are claimed. A 200 n mile exclusive economic zone (EEZ) has also been claimed but the limits have not been defined.

#### Headquarters appointments

Commander-in-Chief of the Navy: Admiral Dong Jun Political Commissar of the Navy: Admiral Yuan Huazhi Chief of Naval Staff: To be announced

#### Fleet commanders

Northern Theatre Navy Commander: Vice Admiral Wang Dazhong
Eastern Theatre Navy Commander:
Vice Admiral Wang Zhogcai
Southern Theatre Navy Commander: Vice Admiral Wang Hai

#### Personnel

- 2021: 235,000 officers and men, including 25,000 naval air force, 8–10,000 marines (28,000 in time of war), and
- 28,000 for coastal defence 2 years' national service for sailors afloat; 3 years for those in shore service. Some stay on for up to 15 years.

#### Operational numbers

Because numbers of vessels are kept in operational reserve, the Chinese version of the order of battle tends to show fewer ships than are counted by observers.

Fleets report to joint theatre commands since 2017. The Northern Theatre Fleet is responsible for the defence of the Yellow Sea and Bohai Sea as well as the maritime gateway Yellow Sea and Bohai Sea as well as the maritime gateway to Beijing. The Eastern Theatre Fleet is responsible for the defence of the East China Sea and the Yellow Sea south of Lianyungang, and the north of the Taiwan Strait. The Southern Theatre Fleet is responsible for the South China Sea and the southern part of the Taiwan Strait, including protecting maritime interests in the south, including the Xisha Islands (Paracel Islands) and the Nansha Islands (Spratty Islands). Each of the Northern, Eastern, and Southern fleets has two submarine divisions, four or more destroyer/frigate (DD/FF) units and at least one mine countermeasure vessel (MCMV)

unit. They also have at least one landing division each. All fleets have at least one submarine unit and two Marine brigades.

Northern Theatre Fleet. Major bases: Qingdao (HQ), Lushun, Huludao. Other bases: Dalian, Xiaopingdao (Dalian), Qinhuangdao, Weihai, Chengshan. Qingdao (Guzhenkou, Taolin), Jianggezhuang (Nanyaowan, Laoshan). Eastern Theatre Fleet. Major bases: Ningbo (HQ), Shanghai, Zhoushan. Other bases: Xiangshan, Fujian (Fuzhou), Dinghai, Wusong (Shanghai), Wuhan and Daxie dao. Southern Theatre Fleet. Major bases: Zhanjiang (HQ), Guangzhou, Yulin. Other bases: Beihai, Xiachuan Island, Yalong Bay (Sanya), Shantou Harbour, Angchuanzhou (Stonecutter's Island, Hong Kong).

#### Coast defence

There are semi-fixed sites and mobile coastal defence units equipped with surface-to-surface missiles (SSMs), including the YJ-62 and some with supersonic YJ-12B. There are air defence brigades equipped with HQ-9, HQ-6A, and shortrange missiles and guns. Southern Theatre air defence units can be forward deployed to islands. The PLA further operates coastal defence brigades equipped with artillery and MLRS.

#### Equipment procurement

Although often listed under the name of the designer, equipment has not necessarily been supplied direct from the parent company. It may have been acquired from a third party

#### Training

The main training centres are: Dalian: Naval Academy Guangzhou: Naval Arms Command College Qingdao: Submarine Academy Wuhan: Naval Engineering University Nanjing: Naval Command College Yantai: Naval Aeronautical Engineering College Bengbu: Naval School for Non-Commissioned Officers

#### Marines

Structure changed in 2017 and expanding to eight brigades with conversion of four former PLA units (3rd-6th brigade), establishment of new 7th aviation brigade, and merging naval combat divers and amphibious reconnaissance units naval combat divers and amphibious reconnaissance units of existing two brigades into 8th special forces brigade. HQ, PLANMC, Chaozhou, Guangdong region 1st Brigade, Southern Theatre, Zhanjiang, Guangdong, 2nd Brigade, Southern Theatre, Zhanjiang, Guangdong, 3rd Brigade, Eastern Theatre, Jinjiang, Fujian. 4th Brigade, Eastern Theatre, Jieyang, Guangdong. 5th Brigade, Northern Theatre, Laoshan, Shandong. 8th Brigade, Northern Theatre, Haiyang, Shandong. 7th Aviation Brigade, Zhucheng, Shandong. 8th Special Forces Brigade Jialong (Dragons), Sanya, Hainan.

#### Naval air force

With 25,000 officers and men and more than 800 aircraft, this is a considerable naval air force primarily land-based. There

is a total of eight Divisions with 27 Regiments split between the three Fleets

Air bases include: Northern Theatre Fleet: Dalian, Qingdao, Jinxi, Jiyuan,

Northern Theatre Fleet: Danyang, Daishan, Snydan, Laiyang, Jiaoxian, Xingtai, Laishan, Anyang, Changzhi, Liangxiang and Shan Hai Guan.
Eastern Theatre Fleet: Danyang, Daishan, Shanghai (Dachang), Ningbo, Luqiao, Feidong and Shitangqiao.
Southern Theatre Fleet: Foluo, Haikou, Lingshui, Sanya, Guiping, Jialaishi and Lingling.

(2) PLAN nuclear submarines are referred to as Chángzhēng (Long March) plus a number, as well as a pennant. Names and numbers may be assigned to new units after

and reduction of the number of openings in the casing on one boat, which participated in the April 2019 Fleet Review. Several boats have a tube above the upper rudder, which suggests they are equipped with a reelable towed array. Modifications on final pair reported to include updates to sonars, radar, and torpedo armament.

Operational: The boats are based at Yulin-Yalongwan on Hainan. The first operational deterrent patrol may have been conducted in 2016 but has not been confirmed.

JIN CLASS

6/2019, Ships of the World / 1748542

Notes: Following the Type 093/093A/093B (Shang)-class programme, construction of a new Type 095 class is reported to have started, with a view to entering service in the 2020s. The submarine is expected to be a guided-missile attack submarine (SSGN), fitted with a vertical launch system, which would deliver a submarine-based land-attack and anti-ship cruise missile capability. The boats are also likely to reflect technological improvements, with particular regard to noise-quietening, which may include pump-jet propulsors replacing propellers.

Displacement, tonnes: 2,725 surfaced; 3,600 dived Dimensions, metres (feet):  $77.2 \times 8.4 \times 6.7$  (253.3  $\times$  27.6  $\times$  22.0)

Missiles: SSM: YJ-82; inertial guidance and active radar terminal homing to 33.3 km (18 n miles) at Mach 0.9; warhead 165 kg; sea-skimmer. A sub-launched version of

YJ-18 may be carried.

Torpedoes: 6—533 mm bow tubes. Combination of Yu-6: wireguided and active/passive and wake homing; thermal; and Yu-9: wire-guided and active/passive and wake homing; electric. Physical countermeasures: To be announced.

Sonars: Bow-mounted; active/passive search and attack; medium; medium frequency. Flank array; passive search; low frequency. Towed array (on boats completed from 2021). Weapon control systems: To be announced. Programmes: The first of class was launched at Wuchang Shipyard, (central) Wuhan, in May 2004 and underwent extensive trials before the second was launched in 2007. An increased building tempo in 2010 suggested a requirement for new boats to replace older classes. Wuchang appears to be the lead shipyard (at a new site east of Wuhan from about 2018) but some boats have been constructed at Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao, near Shanghai. Designations 039B/C reflect observed major variants rather than official PLAN nomenclature. A total of 17 reported to have been built by 2020, and a total of 25 projected by 2025 according to a 2021 US DoD assessment.

to a 2021 US DoD assessment.

Structure: The boat appears to be a Chinese indigenous design. Shorter and broader than the Song class, it exhibits some of the features of the Russian Kilo class design including a teardrop-shaped hull with a distinctive 'hump' and large fin. The teardrop shape suggests a pressurised double hull construction. The stern of the boat resembles the Song class; the single shaft has a seven-bladed propeller.

The submarine is covered with anechoic tiles. The submarine In e submarine is covered with anechoic tiles. The submarine is believed to incorporate air-independent propulsion using Stirling engine technology. Type 039B commissioned from about 2011 feature flank array sonar and modifications to the sail to improve acoustic performance and addition of a sensor on the sail and deletes the sensor on the forward edge of the sail fitted on 039A boats. Several earlier boats converted to 039B standard. A further improved 039B version launched from late 2013 features further hydrodynamic improvements, including a raked and more curved sail. Further modification noted on a host completed at Mychappin 10,021, and severe noted on a boat completed at Wuchang in 2021, and may be referred to as 039C. Features include an extended aft casing and a larger top rudder section featuring a payout tube, indicating the inclusion of a towed array sonar. The sensor on the forward edge of the sail fitted on 039B variant 2 boats was deleted and the sail features advanced shaping, including a chine.

Operational: Basing: 330–339 in East Sea Fleet; 340–341 in North Sea Fleet. 342–346 in South Sea Fleet.

An unidentified Song-class submarine visited Malaysia January 2017.

## **AIRCRAFT CARRIERS**

**Notes:** (1) The former Russian aircraft carrier *Minsk* is a tourist attraction at Shenzhen and *Kiev* is at a military theme park in Tianjin. (2) Follow-on plans for further carriers have been noted in Chinese press. On 15 March 2018 it was reported that a Type 004 carrier design is expected to be in the order of 90,000-100,000 tonnes, nuclear-powered and equipped with electromagnetic catapults. In late November

2019 it was reported that the Chinese government had put on hold plans for Type 004 construction. Chinese media claims that Type 004 will be equipped with EMALS. (3) As of 2019 about six aircraft carriers were expected by the mid-2030s, with nuclear propulsion a possibility for the later ships. The programme may be subject to delays due to technical constraints.

Builders Nikolayev South/Dalian Shipyard Dalian Shipyard

Laid down 6 Dec 1985

Launched 4 Dec 1988 26 Apr 2017

Commissioned 25 Sep 2012 17 Dec 2019

Tacan: To be announced. IFF: To be announced.
Sonars: To be announced. Weapon control systems: To be announced.

Fixed-wing aircraft: Up to 24 J-15 (16) or 36 (17). Helicopters: Up to 15 helicopter

Programmes: Conventionally powered aircraft carriers. Procurement of an aircraft carrier capability has been a high priority for the Chinese Navy since the 1990s. Ex-Varyag, the second of the Kuznetsov-class was between 70 and 80% complete by early 1993 when building was terminated. Subsequently the ship was bought by China and, having been towed through the Bosporus on 2 November 2001, arrived at Dalian in March 2002. For the following three years, it is likely that a thorough material and technical survey of the ship was conducted in order to develop the detailed work package required to activate the ship and to bring it work package required to activate the ship and to bring it to operational status. The main refit work, which included a substantial rebuild of the Island, was conducted 2005–10. Locally referred to as Type 001. Official confirmation that China's first indigenous carrier was under construction at Dalian was made on 31 December 2015. Since then progress has been rapid and the ship emerged from the graving dock on 26 April 2017 and carried out five sets of trials between May 2018 and March 2019. The design is, locally referred to as Type 002 (initially also Type 001A), fundamentally the same as Liaoning although there are differences to the Island and likely the internal spaces, enabled by building from scratch rather than modifying an existing ship. scratch rather than modifying an existing ship.

**Structure:** The hangar of *Liaoning* is  $183 \times 29.4 \times 7.5$  m and can hold up to 18 Flanker aircraft. There are two starboard side lifts, a ski jump of  $14^\circ$ , and angled deck of  $7^\circ$ . There are four arrester wires. The ship has some 16.5 m of freeboard. four arrester wires. The ship has some 16.5 m of freeboard. The HHG-10 launchers and Type 1130 close-in weapons system (CIWS) are sited on sponsons fore and aft. The dimensions of *Shandong* are very similar to *Liaoning*. The general contour of the flight deck, including the aircraft lifts, is broadly the same although there seem to be some changes to the starboard quarter. The island appears to be some 10 m shorter, to provide increased deck space, and the PAR panels have been repositioned. Modernisation: Liaoning refit at Dalian in 2018–19 included installation of a new air traffic control centre and modifications to sensors.

to sensors.

Operational: Liaoning's sea trials started on 10 August 2011 and the ship was handed over to the PLAN on 23 September 2012, formally commissioning on 25 September 2012. Following the successful recovery of a J-15 aircraft on 20 November 2012, flight integration training began in 2012 and approximately successful recovery of a J-15 aircraft. 2013 and continued through 2014. In 2015, the first group of pilots was certified for operational service and the ship was declared fully operational on 15 November 2016. In May 2018 it was announced that the *Liaoning* carrier group reached its initial operational capability. The ship is based at Yuchi (50 km south of Qingdao). Shandong commenced sea trials in May 2018 and was commissioned on 17 December 2019.

(Scale 1: 1,500), Ian Sturton / 1707322

Structure: Large conventionally powered surface combatants. The ships feature an integrated mast housing a number of flat panel arrays. perational: The principal role of this large scale, high-capability class is likely to be carrier battle group protection, comparable to the 'air-defence commander' role of the US Navy's Ticonderoga-class cruisers. In April 2021 101 joined the escort group for the air-craft carrier Liaoning on a deployment to the Pacific Ocean east of Taiwan. The first batch of eight was completed and commissioned by December 2022. 101–104 assigned to Northern Theatre Fleet; 105–108 assigned to Southern Theatre Fleet. A further batch is expected to equip Eastern Theatre Fleet.

Shenzhen is one of very few PLAN surface combatants

Structure: The ships are a development of the Type 052C destroyers. The principal features of the new class include a development of the Dragon Eye phased array radar, with flat panels compared with the curved ones of the Type 052C, and a new multipurpose vertical launching system (VLS) installed in a grid form, compared to the circular silos fitted to the Type 052C. The VLS is capable of housing SAM, SSM and landatteck missiles. The SAM system is reported. SSM, and land-attack missiles. The SAM system is reported to be an improved version of HHQ-9 and the SSM system is ilikely to be the YJ-18 anti-ship missile and anti-ship ballistic missiles. flight deck and centre-line hangar on which there is a shortflight deck and centre-line hangar on which there is a short-range missile system (HHQ-10). Hull stretch of 4 m noted on Type 052DL, starting with Tangshan, launched July 2018, enabling operation of larger maritime helicopter and designated Type 052DL. New air search antenna (replacing Type 517 Knife Rest) noted on ships launched in mid-2019, providing enhanced detection capability against low RCS

Operational: Basing: South Sea Fleet: 161–165, 172–175. North Sea Fleet: 117–124. East Sea Fleet: 132–134, 154–157. These ships are likely to be key components of PLAN carrier task groups.

Programmes: Guided missile destroyers. The first two ships comprised second phase of the destroyer construction programme, which introduced the long-range HHQ-9 missile system into service. After extensive trials, a second batch of four ships was ordered.

Structure: Appears to share the same basic hull design as the Type 052B destroyers, which in turn are based on the Type 051B (Luhai) class. As well as incorporating stealth features, the design includes a taller forward superstructure in which the four phased array antennas are installed. The helicopter hangar is on the port side of the aft superstructure. The close-in weapons systems (CIWS) are on raised platforms forward and on top of the hangar. The main machinery in the third and subsequent ships includes a Chinese-licensed variant of DA-80 gas turbines (QC-280).

Operational: Basing: 170 and 171 in South Sea Fleet. 150-153 in East Sea Fleet.

Programmes: Large surface combatants with ASuW focus. After prolonged negotiations, a contract was signed in September 1996 for two uncompleted Russian

Sovremenny-class (Project 956E) destroyers. Progress was Sovietnering-cases (Froject soll), destroyers. Frogress was held up for a time because China wanted Ka-28 helicopters included, and the Russians demanded extra payment for the aircraft. Deleted Russian units of the class may have been cannibalised for some equipment. A contract for the procurement of two further ships (Project 956EM) was

signed on 3 January 2002.

Modernisation: Hangzhou (136) arrived at Zhoushan for an extensive refit in 2015, which involved replacing much of extensive ferit in 2015, Winter involved replacing much of the original Russian equipment with Chinese systems. The forward and aft SA-N-7 launchers appear to have been replaced with two 16-cells VLS for HHQ-16, a 24-cell HHQ-10 short range SAM launcher has been installed behind the forward gun turret (which remains the original twin AK-130) and the SS-N-22 has been replaced by YJ-12 AShMs. In common with a number of other PLAN surface combatants, Type 382, 366 and 364 radars have been fitted. Work on Hangzhou was completed by the end of 2019 and the ship re-entered in service by mid 2020. Fuzhou (137) completed a similar upgrade in 2020–21. Work on Taizhou (138) commenced in early 2022. Ningbo (139) may follow in due

course.

Structure: These were the first Chinese warships to have a datalink system. The optronic director is probably a Chinese version of Squeeze Box. The Project 956EM ships (138 and 139) are to a modified design. This included variations in weapon fit including replacement of the AK-630 with 'Kashtan' ClWS (with associated Cross Dome target indication radar) and a reduction to one AK-130 turret forward. The flight deck was also extended.

Operational: 136 arrived in China on 16 February 2000 and 137 in February 2011. SSN-22 test fired on 15 September

137 in February 2001. SS-N-22 test fired on 15 September 2001. 138 was delivered on 28 December 2005 and 139 in late 2006. All four ships are based in the East Sea Fleet.

## **FRIGATES**

Notes: The Type 054B frigate programme is reported to be the next class of frigates to follow the Type 054A (Jiangkai II) programme and the first surface combatant ship programme observed to feature design competition among Chinese shipyards. Around 2017 local sources reported that CSSC submitted a design for a trimaran-hulled frigate concept while CSIC Group presented a more conventional ship, with the latter eventually selected. Features includes expanded aviation facilities compared to Type 054A, a new anti-submarine sonar, and hybrid propulsion. A class of 20 ships is expected. Unconfirmed reports indicate work on the first ship may have started in May 2022.

#### SHIPBORNE AIRCRAFT

Notes: (1) Two variants of the CAIG Z-18 troop-carrying helicopter are reported to be under development for the Chinese Navy. The aircraft, which appear to be based on the Z-8 Super Frelon, are too large for destroyers and frigates and are likely to be intended for carrier operations. An anti-submarine warfare variant, known as Z-18F, features a redesigned cockpit operations. An anti-submarine warfare variant, known as Z-18f, features a redesigned cockpit and modified hull form and is equipped with a dipping sonar. Reports suggest that it can carry up to 32 sonobuoys and four lightweight torpedoes such as the Yu-7. It has a prominent chin-mounted surface search radar and it is probable that the aircraft is fitted with a datalink for third-party targeting. An airborne early warning variant, known as Z-18J, which has a swing-down radar antenna fitted in place of the loading ramp, have been photographed on Liaoning's flight deck. Both aircraft are likely to be deployed to the carriers in due course and a typical air-wing might include four airborne electronic warfare (AEW) and four anti-submarine warfare (ASW) helicopters, although actual numbers would be based on prevailing tactical requirements. (2) A naval variant of the Z-20 10-tonne class helicopter is reported to be under development. (2) A naval variant of the Z-20 10-tonne class helicopter is reported to be under development. The aircraft is externally similar to the Sikorsky S-70.

Numbers/Type: 38 CAIG Z-8 Super Frelon.
Operational speed: 134 kt (248 km/h).
Service ceiling: 10,000 ft (3,050 m).
Range: 440 n miles (815 km).
Role/Weapon systems: Anti-submarine warfare (ASW), anti-surface (ASW), Medivac and SAR roles. Derived from SA 321G Super Frelon initially supplied from France in 1977.
14 ASW/ASWW (Z-8J), 4 Medivac (Z-8JH), and about 20 utility (Z-8) believed to be in-service.
Operate from shore or amphibious ships. Deployed on Type 071 LPH for counter piracy operations in 2010, 2013, and 2014. Sensors: surface search radar, Thomson-Sintra HS-12 dipping sonar. Some aircraft fitted with FLIR turret. Weapons: ASW: lightweight torpedoes (Yu-7), ASuW: YJ-83K missile, rockets, and machine guns.

![](_page_19_Picture_12.jpeg)

1/2015, Derek Fox / 1629716

Numbers/Type: 22/22 HAIG Z-9C/9D (Haitun). Operational speed: 134 kt (248 km/h). Service ceiling: 14,100 ft (4,300 m). Range: 236 n miles (437 km).

Range: 236 n miles (437 km).

Role/Weapon systems: ASW (Z-9C), ASuW (Z-9D) and SAR. Licensed assembly of 50 Aerospatiale AS365N Dauphin/AS565MA Panther for PLA and PLAN commenced 1980. Production by HAIG commenced 1988. Z-9C ASW variant may carry dipping sonar or torpedoes but not both. Some aircraft equipped with dipping sonar similar in appearance to Helras sonar. Aircraft adapted for SAR role fitted with EO turret (TV and FLIR), searchlight and winch. Aircraft deployed on counter-piracy operations may be fitted with 12.7 mm machine gun and 57 mm rocket launcher. Z-9D anti-ship variant capable of carrying 4 short range AShMs. Widely deployed on Type 054A frigates. Sensors: Thomson-CSF Agrion-15 or KLC-1 surface search I/J-band radar; Thomson-Sintra HS-12 or Type 605 dipping sonar. Weapons: ASW: 2 lightweight torpedoes (Yu-7). ASuW: 4 KJ-10B anti-ship missiles.

Numbers/Type: 14/3 Kamov Ka-28 Helix A/D. Operational speed: 135 kt (250 km/h). Service ceiling: 19,685 ft (6,000 m). Range: 432 n miles (800 km).

Hange: 432 n miles (800 km).
Role/Weapon systems: ASW (Ka-28 PL) and SAR (Ka-28PS). Six ASW and three SAR aircraft acquired in late 90s. Further eight ASW aircraft procured in 2009. Numbers/Type: 22 SAC J-15 (Flying Shark). Operational speed: 1,240 kt (2,296 km/h). Service ceiling: 55,700 ft (16,977 m).

Range: 1,600 n miles (2,963 km).

Role/Weapon systems: Primary role training aircrew for carrier operations. Derivative of Su-33 and development of J-11B. Maiden flight 2009, first carrier deck landings/take-offs (ski-jump) October/November 2012. Seven prototypes and 24 production aircraft manufactured by end 2017, although two aircraft lost in accidents. Tandem two-seat trainer (J-15S) began flight testing November 2012. Catapult capable variant with modified nose wheel under development and being used on catapult trials facilities at Huangdicun airbase. EW variant possibly also under development and new wingtip EW pod noted about April 2018. 12 hardpoints for external stores. Weapons: ASuW: YJ-83K and YJ-91A AShM and YJ-91 anti-radiation missile (ARM) can be carried.

Interim capability for fleet protection prior to future carrier-borne fixed-wing AEW. E-801M Oko early warning radar, detection out to 200 km.

## **LAND-BASED MARITIME AIRCRAFT (FRONT LINE)**

Notes: In addition to those listed there are more than 100 training and transport aircraft.

Numbers/Type: 4 KJ-2000 AEW&C. Service ceiling: 34,440 ft (10,500 m). Range: 2,753 n miles (5,100 km).

Role/Weapon systems: Airborne Early Warning and Control (AEW&C). System (AWACS) Aircraft based on the Russian-made A-50 (Mainstay) airframe which itself is based on the Ilyushin II-76 transport aircraft. Operated by the PLAAF from Wuxi airbase. The non-rotating radome houses three NRIET active electronically scanned arrays, installed in a triangular configuration. Satcom antenna housed in dorsal blister forward of wing.

Numbers/Type: 22 Sukhoi Su-30 MK2 (Flanker).

Operational speed: 1,144 kt (2,119 km/h). Service ceiling: 56,760 ft (17,300 m). Range: 1,620 n miles (3,000 km).

Role/Weapon systems: Two-seat long range maritime-strike fighter. 24 delivered to PLANAF in 2004. Sensors: Two-channel fire-control radar. Weapons: Up to 10 AAMs, including PL-12. Kh-31A/P AShM/ARM or local variants YJ-91/YJ-91A.

Numbers/Type: 54/66 XAC JH-7/JH-7A Operational speed: 653 kt (1,210 km/h) Service ceiling: 51,180 ft (15,600 m). Range: 891 n miles (1,650 km).

Role/Weapon systems: All-weather tandem seat maritime multirole fighter bomber. Entered service with PLANAF in 1998; upgraded JH-7A delivered from 2004. Sensors: Letri JL-10A Shen-Ying pulse Doppler fire-control radar capable of tracking four targets to 29 n miles (54 km) in look-down mode simultaneously. Weapons: 11 external hardpoints. AAM: PL-5b, PL-8 and 23 mm gun. ASuW: YJ-81, YJ-83K, KD-88 or YJ-91A anti-ship missiles. LGBs, rocket pods, aerial mines, and ECM pods may also be carried.

Numbers/Type: 23/7 SAC Y-8/Y-9 surveillance aircraft. Operational speed: 297 kt (550 km/h).

Service ceiling: 34,120 ft (10,400 m). Range: 3,020 n miles (5,600 km).

Range: 3,020 n miles (s,000 km).

Role/Weapon systems: Derivative of Antonov An-12 Cub transport; first flown 1985.

Development programme for special mission aircraft, known as Gao Xin (GX) (New High).

Y-8X: three aircraft equipped with Litton APS-504(Y)3 radar, Y-8J: four aircraft for patrol and airborne early warning. Y-8JB (GX-2): four aircraft equipped for ELINT operations. Y-8Q/KQ-200 (GX-6): MPA with chin-mounted surface search radar and distinctive MAD tail boom; inservice numbers growing as platform in serial production. Y-9JB (GX-8): 7 ELINT-equipped aircraft based on improved platform (Y-9).

#### 60 HOUBEI (TYPE 22) CLASS

(FAST ATTACK CRAFT-MISSILE) (PGGF)

2308-2331

Displacement, tonnes: 220 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $42.6 \times 12.2 \times 1.5$  (139.8 × 40.0 × 4.9)

Speed, knots: 40 Complement: 12

Machinery: 4 diesels: 4 Kamewa waterjets

Missiles: 8 YJ-83J (CSS-N-8 Saccade) (2 quad); inertial guidance and active radar homing to 180 km (97.2 n miles) at Mach 0.9; warhead 165 kg or 190 kg; sea skimmer.

Guns: 1 H/PJ-13 30 mm/65 (AK-630M); 6 barrels per mounting; 5,000 rds/min combined to 4 km (2.2 n miles).

Radars: Surface search: Type 348 (LR 66); I-band.

Navigation: I-band.

Weapon control systems: Optronic director.

Comment: The first craft (2208) was launched at Qiuxin Shipyard, Shanghai in April 2004. The design is believed to be based on a 42 m hull developed by AMD Marine Consulting, Sydney. This was further progressed by its joint venture company in Guangzhou, Sea Bus International (SBI), into a patrol boat configuration, which was selected by the Chinese Navy after a five-year investigation into various platform contenders. The craft has a wave-piercing catamaran hull form and a centre bow. Likely to be of aluminium alloy construction, the design incorporates some radar cross section (RCS) reduction measures. Following extensive first of class trials, full production was reported to have taken place in at least six shipyards. or class trials, full production was reported to have taken place in at least six shipyards. Production ceased in 2009. Dimensions are based on the original AMD design. The mismatch in range of the YJ-83J and maximum radar range suggests a datalink is fitted to facilitate over-the-horizon targeting. The craft are based in all three fleets and are likely to use a sector-defence concept, operating in squadrons of eight craft. Basing: 2101–2112 (North); 2208–2231 (East); 2308–2331 (South). Unconfirmed reports indicate some are laid up, however, there are also indications that this is related to galvanic corrosion prevention measures.

## **AMPHIBIOUS FORCES**

Notes: (1) There are plans for a new, larger LHD class under project tender 'XX6'. The Type 076 LHD is expected to be in the 35–45,000 tonne range. Inclusion of an Electromagnetic Aircraft Launch System (EMALS) enabling embarkation of fixed-wing UAVs and UCAVs is a possibility. The propulsion system is reported to include gas turbines and diesel engines. A class of six units is estimated by 2030 (about two per PLAN fleet).

(2) In addition to the ships listed there are up to 500 minor LCM/LCVP types used to transport

## 25 YUPEN (TYPE 271) CLASS (LANDING CRAFT) (LCU)

Displacement, tonnes: 610 standard; 800 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $56.5 \times 10.4 \times 2.3$  (185.4  $\times$  34.1  $\times$  7.5) Speed, knots: 13 Complement: 25

Military lift: 3 tanks, 200 troops, or 150 tonnes Machinery: 2 diesels; 2,250 hp (1.7 MW); 2 shafts Guns: 8—14.5 mm (4 twin).

Radars: Navigation: I-band.

Comment: Utility landing craft widely used for the transport of troops, vehicles and stores. Construction is reported to have started in 1968 and the first variant (Type 271I) entered service in about 1970 and this was followed in 1972–78 by Type 271II and in the late 1980s by Type 271III. Building continued in the 1990s to replace decommissioned craft but current numbers are approximate. Details are based on the latest generation of craft. Variants also in use by the army (pennants prefixed by two letters) and air force (pennant prefixed by K).

![](_page_22_Picture_39.jpeg)

![](_page_23_Picture_13.jpeg)

YIMENG SHAN

4/2018, Kürsener Collection / 1724284

Programmes: Landing platform dock type amphibious warfare ships. After several years' speculation, the existence of the programme was confirmed when construction of the first of class was initiated in mid-2006. The programme constitutes a key component of the PLAN's plan to improve its sealift and power projection capabilities. Eight ships have been completed with more expected. been completed with more expected.

Structure: The principal features of the design include a large well deck area to accommodate four Type 726 ACVs in the aft two-thirds of the ship. The ACVs access the ship through a stern gate. There is a large helicopter flight deck aft and an extensive hangar for up to four Z-8 size helicopters. An internal garage deck for vehicles can be accessed via side ramps (port and starboard). Two LCVPs are carried.

Operational: Four are based at Zhanjiang (South Sea Fleet). The fourth and fifth are allocated to the East Sea

Sales: One ordered by Thailand on 9 September 2019.

full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $120 \times 16.4 \times 3.2$  (393.7  $\times$  53.8  $\times$  10.5) Speed, knots: 17. Range, n miles: 3,000 at 14 kt Complement: 120

Military lift: 250 troops; 10 tanks; 4 LCVP

(5.1 n miles); weight of shell 0.73 kg. Batch 2 (2015 on): 1 H/PJ-17 30 mm; 350 rds/min to
3 km (1.6 n miles).

Comment: Improved version of the Type 072III (Yuting I) class with similar dimensions. Design differences include modifications to the stern, including the ramp and a taller funnel. A tunnel in the centre of the superstructure connects the main and after decks, facilitating onload/offload. First batch of nine built 2002–05; second batch 2014–16. 992–997 based in the South Sea Fleet; 911 and 912 in the North and 913-917, 981-982 in the East.

## 20 YUNNAN (TYPE 067) CLASS (LCU)

Displacement, tonnes: 85 standard; 135 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $28.6\times5.4\times1.5$  (93.8  $\times$  17.7  $\times$  4.9) Speed, knots: 12

Range, n miles: 500 at 10 kt Complement: 12

Military lift: 1 tank or 2 armoured vehicles or 46 tonnes Machinery: 2—12V150 diesels; 600 hp(m) (441 kW); 2 shafts Radars: Navigation: I-band.

Comment: Built in China 1968–72 although a continuing programme was reported in 1982. One to Sri Lanka in 1991 and a second in 1995. Two units noted in Tanzania and one in Cambodia. Most are estimated to be in reserve or non-front line use and units of the type also reported to have converted for buoy and cable-laying tasks. Some may have 12.7 mm MGs. Total number uncertain and estimated about 20 as of 2023.

#### 4 + 2 POMORNIK (ZUBR) (PROJECT 1232.2) (TYPE 958) CLASS (ACVM/LCUJM)

| No   | Builders                    | Commissioned |
|------|-----------------------------|--------------|
| 3325 | Feodosiya Shipbuilding Co   | 2015         |
| 3326 | Feodosiya Shipbuilding Co   | 2015         |
| 3327 | Huangpu Shipyard, Guangzhou | 2017         |
| 3328 | Huangpu Shipyard, Guangzhou | 2018         |

Displacement, tonnes: 550 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet): 57.6 × 25.6 (189.0 × 84.0)

Speed, knots: 63

Range, n miles: 300 at 55 kt Complement: 31 (4 officers)

Military lift: 3 MBT or 10 APC plus 230 troops (total 130 tonnes)

Machinery: 5 Zorya-Mashproekt DP-71 gas turbines; two for lift; 20,000 hp (15 MW); three for drive: 30,000 hp (22.4 MW)

Missiles: SAM: 9K32 Strela-2 (SA-N-5 Grail); 2 quad launchers for 9M32 missiles; manual

aiming, IR homing to 2.2 km (1.2 n miles) at Mach 1.26; altitude up to 1,500; warhe 1.17 kg.

Guns: 2 AK-630M 30 mm/65; 6 barrels per mounting; 5,000 rds/min combined to 4 km

(2.2 n miles); weight of shell 0.39 kg.

Rockets: 2 A-22 Ogon 140 mm; 22-barrelled rocket launchers.

Mines: 2 rails can be carried for 80.

Physical countermeasures: Decoys: MS227 chaff launcher.
Electronic countermeasures: ESM: Tool Box; intercept.
Radars: Surface search: Curl Stone; I-band.

Fire control: MR-123 Vympel/Bagira (Bass Tilt); I-band. IFF: Salt Pot A/B. Square Head.

Weapon control systems: Quad Look (DWU-3) (modified Squeeze Box) optronic director

Comment: Negotiations with Almaz, St Petersburg, for the procurement of the world's largest air cushion landing craft were first reported during 2005. Discussions with Ukraine were opened in 2008 and it was announced on 7 August 2009 that four vessels were to be procured, with the first two to be constructed at Morye Shipyard, Ukraine and the second two in China under licence. The first of class was delivered by heavy lift ship in November 2012 and the second in March 2014. Construction of the first locally assembled version at the Huangpu shipyard in Guangzhou took a protracted period. This is likely to have been a consequence of the Russian annexation of the Crimea (including Feodosiya), with Russia and China apparently negotiating a new agreement although many parts are manufactured. consequence of the russial amexation of the crimea (including a cools) and China apparently negotiating a new agreement, although many parts are manufactured in Ukraine. The first domestic craft successfully completed sea trials in March 2017. Construction of at least one additional craft is reported to have started in China about 2017. however, has been delayed. Note: details of the craft are as for those in Russian service and Chinese specifications may be different.

#### 12 PAYI (TYPE 724) CLASS (LANDING CRAFT-AIR CUSHION) (LCAC)

3310-3312

8530-8538

Displacement, tonnes: 6.5 standard Dimensions, metres (feet): 12.4 on cushion  $\times$  4.7 (40.7  $\times$  15.4)

Speed, knots: 40. Range, n miles: 100 at 35 kt Complement: 3 (est)

Military lift: 10 troops Machinery: 2 BF12L913C diesels; 760 hp (566 kW)

Comment: A class of small air cushion landing craft design, which entered service from 1994. The craft are operated from the Yukan and Yuting classes of LST. The Type 724 LCAC has three compartments: a space for 10 troops in an unprotected area forward, a control compartment in the middle, and engine room aft. Two diesels provide power to drive the air-cushion blowers and the air propellers are located within ring shrouds at the stern. Additional units reported and overall numbers uncertain.

Displacement, tonnes: 650 standard; 800 full load (est) Dimensions, metres (feet):  $65.0 \times 11.0 \times 2.7$  ( $213.3 \times 36.1 \times 8.9$ ) Military lift: 3 Type 96 MBTs or 6 IFVs or 250 troops or 150 tonnes cargo Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts Guns: 4-14.5 mm (2 twin).

Comment: Built at Qingdao, Zhanjiang, Shanghai and Dinghai. Monohull design with twin bow, folding bow ramp, superstructure on starboard side and single central vehicle lane on deck. Two anchors forward, one aft. Waterline exhausts. One craft was damaged by Typhoon Rammasun in July 2014. Basing: 3128 and 3129 in the North Sea Fleet; 3232–35 in the South Sea Fleet; 3315–3318 in the East Sea Fleet.

# 21 YUYI (TYPE 726A) CLASS

(LANDING CRAFT-AIR CUSHION) (LCAC)

| No   | Builders                        | Commissioned |
|------|---------------------------------|--------------|
| 3320 | Qiuxin Shipyard                 | _            |
| 3321 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3322 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3330 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | -            |
| 3331 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3332 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3333 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3334 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | _            |
| 3236 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | 10 Jan 2018  |
| 3237 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | 10 Jan 2018  |
| 3238 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | 10 Jan 2018  |
| 3239 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | 10 Jan 2018  |

Displacement, tonnes: 170 full load Dimensions, metres (feet): 33.0 on cushion  $\times$  16.8 (108.3  $\times$  55.1)

Speed, knots: 40

Range, n miles: 200 at 40 kt

Military lift: Armoured fighting vehicle plus troops or 60 tonnes approx Machinery: Type 726A: 2 QC-70 gas turbines for propulsion and lift; 18,775 hp (14 MW); 2 shrouded reversible-pitch airscrews (propulsion)

Radars: Surface search/navigation: I-band.

Comment: A class of air cushion landing craft (LCAC) design, intended for operation from the Yuzhao (Type 071) class LPD. The craft appears to be similar to but larger than the US Navy LCAC. The vehicle is capable of transporting two ZBD-05 amphibious assault vehicles (AAVs) and troops. In contrast to the US Navy LCAC, the driving/command module is located on the port side instead of the starboard side. The main cargo deck is about 5 m wide and there are bow and stern ramps. Propulsion is provided by two 4 m shrouded reversible-pitch propulsing. The first vessel was built at 0 living Shirward and launched in 2000 with the propellers. The first vessel was built at Qiuxin Shipyard and launched in 2009, with two further craft observed at Jiangnan Changxingdao Shipyard in 2013. This first batch was reported to be powered by Ukrainian UGT6000 gas turbines. In 2015 a modified second batch was built, powered by QC-70 gas turbines, and denoted as Type 726A. Intial batch reported to have been modified to Type 726A standard. In November 2017 satellite imagery of Jiangnan Changxingdao Shipyard showed five more Type 726As nearing completion. More than 20 reported in service by December 2019. More than 20 reported in service by December 2019

#### MINE WARFARE FORCES

Notes: Six Type 529 (Wonang)-class 30 m (about 50 tonne) drone minesweepers (8041, 8042, 8043, 8181, 8182, 8183) are known to be in service, based in the East Sea Fleet. They entered service in 2010 and are controlled by Type 082 II (Wozang)-class MCMVs. Three unmanned minesweepers appear to be assigned to each MCMV mothership as denoted by first three numbers of the pennant number. Additional Type 529 craft may also have been built in line with increasing numbers of Time 083 II MCMVs. increasing number of Type 082 II MCMVs.

## 6 DONGDJIAN (TYPE 927) CLASS (OCEAN SURVEILLANCE SHIPS) (AGOSH)

| Name | No  | Builders         | Launched    | Commissioned |
|------|-----|------------------|-------------|--------------|
| -    | 780 | Huangpu Shipyard | Jun 2017    | 2018         |
| -    | 781 | Wuchang Shangliu | 21 Mar 2018 | 2019         |
| -    | 782 | Huangpu Shipyard | 27 Mar 2018 | 2019         |
| _    | 783 | Huangpu Shipyard | 2020        | Aug 2021     |
| -    | -   | Wuchang Shangliu | 2020        | 2022         |
| _    | -   | Bohai Shipyard   | Mar 2021    | 2022         |

Displacement, tonnes: 5,000 full load (est) Dimensions, metres (feet): 90 (est)  $\times$  30  $\times$  ? (295.3  $\times$  98.4  $\times$  ?)

Machinery: To be announced Radars: To be announced.

Sonars: Active/passive towed array sonar.

Comment: The Type 927 SWATH vessels of about 90 m length and 5,000 tonnes are similar to the *Ruili 10* hydroacoustic surveillance ship launched at Wuchang Shipbuilding on 12 April 2016 and operated by the Hangzhou Institute of Applied Acoustics (715th Research Institute). Also appear to be superficially similar to the USNS *Impeccable* and Japanese Hibiki class. The vessels appear to have underwater surveillance as their primary role. Equipped with flight deck aft. First ship (780) was reported fitting out at Huangpu Shipyard, Guangzhou, in June 2017. A second ship (781) was launched at Wuchang Shuangliu in March 2018, and a third at Huangpu Shipyard in March 2018. A fourth was launched at Huangpu Shipyard in 2020, and a fifth had been set afloat at Wuchang Shuangliu by January 2021. A further, stretched, unit has been noted at Bohai Shipyard after launch around February/ March 2021.

Displacement, tonnes: 1,500 (Bei Diao 990–991); 1,350 (Bei Ce 901–902, Dong Ce 232–233, Nan Ce 429–430) full load

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $60 \times 18 \times ?$  (196.9  $\times 59.1 \times ?$ ) Machinery: Diesel-electric; 2 shafts

Comment: SWATH design ocean surveillance ships of about 60 m length. First launched in September 2007. Two had been completed by the end of 2009. Acoustic sensors lowered through a well between the hulls. Improved version (Type 639A) was delivered from 2012, which features changes to the hull and superstructure and deletes the well, featuring instead facilities for launch and retrieval of sensors at the stern. In October 2015 imagery indicated use of active/passive towed array sensor similar to those fitted on surface combatants. Basing: 990, 991, 901, 902 in the North. 429 and 430 in the South. 232 and 233 in the Fast 233 in the East.

## SURVEY AND RESEARCH SHIPS

Notes: (1) The Xiangyanghong series are research vessels operated by China's State Oceanic Notes: (1) The Xiangyanghong series are research vessels operated by China's State Oceanic Administration. Many have recently been replaced by new vessels of the same name, including Xiangyanghong 01 (2016, 4,864 GT), Xiangyanghong 03 (2016, 4,864 GT), Xiangyanghong 06, Xiangyanghong 07, Xiangyanghong 08 (2008, 600 GT), Xiangyanghong 10 (2014, 4,500 GT), Xiangyanghong 14 (1981, 3,141 GT), Xiangyanghong 16, Xiangyanghong 18 (2015, 2,200 tonnes), Xiangyanghong 19 (2011, 3,216 GT), Xiangyanghong 20 (2014, 3,160 tonnes), Xiangyanghong 28, Xiangyanghong 29 (2014, 1,200 tonnes), Xiangyanghong 52 (1975, 1,175 GT), and Xiangyanghong 81 (2015, 300 GT).

(2) A further SWATH hydroacoustic surveillance ship of about 5,300 tonnes, 82 m length and 32 m beam similar to the Type 927 units, *Ruili 10*, was launched by Wuchang Shipbuilding on 12 April 2016. Operated by the Hangzhou Institute of Applied Acoustics (715th Research Institute).

## 2 DAHUA (TYPE 909/909A) CLASS (AGE/AGEH)

Builders Commissioned BI SHENG HUA LUOGENG 851 (ex-970, ex-909) 852 (ex-892) Hudong-Zhonghua, Shanghai Hudong-Zhonghua, Shanghai Dec 1997 2012

Speed, knots: 20

Complement: 80 Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts

Helicopters: Platform (891) for one medium.

Comment: Weapons trials ships equipped to test a number of the PLAN's modern radars and missiles, such as Type 346/346A AESA radars, HHQ-9 vertically launched AAW missiles, and HHQ-10 short-range air-defence system. Launcher for HHQ-10 installed on flight deck of Hua Luogeng. A new search radar was noted to have been installed by January 2020. Changes to appearance of superstructure reflect systems under test. The second ship entered service 15 years after Bi Sheng and designated Type 909A.

Comment: A second-generation space tracking ship commissioned in April 1995 and given a major upgrade in 2006. Equipped with E/F-band tracking radar for monitoring launches of satellites and also Shenzhou manned spacecraft. Positioned to provide tracking coverage able from Chinese land-based tracking stations, typically mid-Atlantic or mid-Pacific Based at Jiangyin on Yangtze River.

## 3 YUANWANG III CLASS (SPACE EVENT SHIPS) (AGMH)

| Name       | Builders                        | Launched    | Commissioned |
|------------|---------------------------------|-------------|--------------|
| YUANWANG 5 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Shanghai     | 15 Sep 2006 | 29 Sep 2007  |
| YUANWANG 6 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Shanghai     | 16 Mar 2007 | 12 Apr 2008  |
| YUANWANG 7 | Jiangnan Shipyard, Changxingdao | 15 Oct 2015 | 12 Jul 2016  |

Measurement: 22,686 gt

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $222.2 \times 25.2 \times 8.2$  (729.0  $\times$  82.7  $\times$  26.9)

Speed, knots: 20

Range, n miles: 20,000 at 12 kt

Machinery: 2 Wärtsilä 8L 46C diesels; 31,078 hp (22.86 MW); 2 shafts

Helicopters: 1 medium.

Comment: China's third-generation of space tracking ships. Yuanwang 6 reportedly differs from Yuanwang 5 in that it includes a large mission control hall occupying two decks. The ships are equipped with E/F-band and G-band monopulse tracking radars. They are also fitted with a range of meteorological instruments including weather radar, radiosonde, and weather balloons. Some differences in superstructure and antennas layout between ships. Based at Jiangyin on Yangtze River.

## DEEP SUBMERGENCE VEHICLES

## 1 LR 7 RESCUE SUBMERSIBLE (RESCUE VEHICLES) (DSRV)

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $9.7\times3.2\times3.4$  (31.8  $\times$  10.5  $\times$  11.2) Speed, knots: 3.5

Complement: 3

Machinery: 2 electric propulsors; 26.8 hp (20 kW); 3 supplementary thrusters; 16 hp (12 kW)

Comment: Power drawn from two external battery pods, the Perry Slingsby LR 7 is a development of the LR 5 rescue submersible, originally built for North Sea commercial operations and subsequently purchased by the Royal Navy for submarine rescue operations. Capable of operating down to 500 m depth, it will be deployed from a Type 926 (Dalao class) ASR, three of which are in service. Its role is to rescue up to 18 survivors at a time from a disabled submarine on the seabed and bring them back to the surface. This can be done at disabled submarine on the seabled and oring them back to the surface. This can be dolled an ormal atmospheric pressure or at increased pressure up to 5 bar. Mating can be achieved with the disabled submarine at up to 60° bow up. Following tests in Scotland, LR 7 entered service in the PLA Navy in 2009. Type 926 ASR *Changda* (867) deployed to Vladivostock in September 2017 with LR 7 embarked to conduct submarine rescue training with the Russian Navy and LR 7 was reported to have mated with a Russian Kilo class simulating a distressed

Dimensions, metres (feet): 14.9  $\times$  2.6  $\times$  2.6  $(48.9 \times 8.5 \times 8.5)$  Speed, knots: 4

Complement: 3

DSRV

Machinery: 2 silver-zinc batteries; 1 motor; 1 shaft

Comment: Construction of first vessel at Wuchang Shipyard in Wuhan commenced in 1976 and completed sea trials in 1986. Deployed on Type 925 (Dajiang class) submarine support ships. Capable of 'wet' rescue at 300 m and of diving to 600 m. Capacity for up to 22 survivors. Underwater TV, high-frequency active sonar and a manipulator arm are all fitted. Life support duration is 1,728 man-hours. Modernised by 1996. Superseded in DSRV role by LR 7 rescue vehicle.

![](_page_27_Picture_69.jpeg)

1991, CSSC / 0056786

## 1 DASHI (TYPE 0891A) CLASS (HSS/AHH)

Name SHICHANG Builders Qiuxin, Shanghai

Displacement, tonnes: 10,000 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $120 \times 18 \times 7$  (393.7  $\times$  59.1  $\times$  23.0) Speed, knots: 17.5

Range, n miles: 8,000 at 17 kt Complement: 370 (200 trainees) Military lift: 300 containers Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts Helicopters: Platform only. 2 spots.

Comment: Multirole ship officially described as a defence mobilisation vessel. Up to 300 ISO containers can be loaded onto weather deck in two layers. Can be used for civilian freight, for helicopter or navigation training, or as a hospital ship. The vessel looks like a scaled down version of the UK Argus with the bridge superstructure forward and an after funnel on the starboard side of the flight deck. Helicopter training modules include temporary hangar. There are two landing spots. Medical modules may include operating theatres, wards, and X-ray facilities. Assigned to the Naval Academy in Dalian. Based in the North Sea Fleet.

Comment: A new training ship was launched at Liaonan Shipyard, Lushun, in about September 2016. Design features include a large lecture theatre, a gymnasium, and a ship handling simulator. The ship is also equipped with a large flight deck (but no hangar) aft. The ship sailed from Lushun in September 2017 for a three month deplayment without the large flight deck (but no hangar) aft. The ship sailed from Lushun in September 2017 for a three-month deployment, visiting Italy, Portugal, Sri Lanka, and Thailand

Displacement, tonnes: 48,000 full load (est) Dimensions, metres (feet):  $241\times32\times10.8$  (790.7  $\times$  105.0  $\times$  35.4)

Military lift: 20,000 tonnes dieso; 5,000 tonnes avgas; 1,000 tonnes potable water; 3,000 tonnes ammunition; 500 tonnes dry cargo
Machinery: CODAD; 4 Shaanxi SEMT-Pielstick 16PC2.6 diesels; 2 shafts
Guns: 4 H/PJ-13 30 mm/65 (AK-630M); 6 barrels per mounting; 5,000 rds/min combined to 4 km (2,2 n miles).

Radars: Air search: Type 363S (Sea Tiger); E/F-band Air/surface search: Type 364 (Seagull C); G/H/I/J-bands. Navigation: 1 E/F-band. 2 I-band.

Fire-control: I-band (for 30 mm)

Weapon control systems: 1 optronic director (for 30 mm).

Helicopters: 2 Z-8 or Z-18.

Comment: The first of a new class of combat support ship was launched at Guangzhou comment: The first of a new class of combat support ship was launched at Guangzhou Shipyard International's Longxue (Nansha) yard on 15 December 2015. The ship is expected to have a carrier support role and to be capable of under way replenishment of fuel oil for-propulsion, aviation fuel, air-launched weapons, general stores, and victuals. The ship is equipped with three gantries each side and a fourth high-point structure port side aft. Overall there are five hose rigs for liquid refuelling on the port side and four on the starboard side. The central gantry provides a transfer station for solids on each side. Replenishment of solids is expected to include food and equipment spares, as well as air-launched weapons. Design features also include a large flight deck and two hangars enabling embarkation of aircraft such as the Z-8/Z-18 medium-lift helicopters. The ship was commissioned in September 2017. A second ship was launched in June 2017 and commissioned in December 2018. Pennant numbers revised from 2021.

#### 3 DANYAO I/II (TYPE 904A/904B) CLASS (SUPPORT SHIP) (AFH)

| Name             | No  | Builders                                     | Laid down | Launched    | Commissioned |
|------------------|-----|----------------------------------------------|-----------|-------------|--------------|
| <b>FUXIAN HU</b> | 888 | Guangzhou Shipyard<br>International, Shangha | 2005<br>i | 28 Dec 2006 | 23 Aug 2007  |
| JUNSHAN HU       | 961 | Guangzhou Shipyard<br>International          | 2013      | 30 Jan 2015 | 10 Jul 2015  |
| LUGU HU          | 962 | Guangzhou Shipyard                           | 2013      | 25 Mar 2015 | 26 Dec 2015  |

Displacement, tonnes: 15,000 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $165 \times 19.1 \times 9.0$  ( $541.3 \times 62.7 \times 29.5$ )

Machinery: 2 Shaanxi SEMT-Pielstick 16PC2.6V-400 diesels; 24,000 hp (17.9 MW); 2 shafts

Guns: Type 904A: 4 H/PJ-76F 37 mm (2 twin) 400 rds/min to 9.4 km (5.1 n miles); weight of shell 0.73 kg. 4 Type 61 25 mm/60 (2 twin). Type 904B: 2 H/PJ-17 30 mm; 350 rds/min to 3 km (1.6 n miles)

Helicopters: Type 904A: Platform for one medium. Type 904B: Z-8 or Ka-28.

Comment: Logistics support ships for island garrison resupply, likely to operate primarily in South China Sea. Type 904A entered service in 2007. Larger than Dayun class (Type 904) and equipped with two prominent pairs of large davits midships, to deploy boats/landing craft to ferry stores and personnel ashore. Design includes a flight deck. In 2009 the ship transferred to the Fishery Law Enforcement Command (FLEC) and changed its pennant number to 88 before returning to naval service in the South Sea Fleet. Two further ships (961, 962) entered service in 2015 to a modified design (Type 904B). Most significant change is provision of a hangar to enable a helicopter to be embarked. Distinguishable from Type 904A by twin funnels, connected by lattice structure to support aft mast.

#### 1 + 1 ANWEI (TYPE 920) (HOSPITAL SHIP) (AHH)

Launched Commissioned DAISHAN DAO 866 Guangzhou Shipyard 2006 29 Aug 2007 22 Dec 2008

Displacement, tonnes: 14,200 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $178.0 \times 24.0 \times 6.8$  (584.0  $\times$  78.7  $\times$  22.3) Speed, knots: 20

Range, n miles: 10.000 at 14 kt

Complement: 135 Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts; bow thruster

Radars: Navigation: E/F/I-bands. Helicopters: 1 Z-8JH.

Comment: The first purpose-built hospital ship for the Chinese Navy was launched in August 2007 and commissioned in 2008. Known as the Peace Ark, the ship is based at Zhoushan (East Sea Fleet). Fitted with a flight deck and hangar, it can embark and operate the Z-8JH medivac helicopter. The ship is equipped with eight operating theatres and has deployed extensively to developing countries providing free medical treatment. 'Harmony Mission 2017' encompassed Angola, Democratic Republic of Congo, Dijibouti, Gabon, Mozambique, Sierra Leone, Tanzania, and Timor-Leste, where a total of more than 60,000 people were given treatment. A second ship observed under construction in 2022.

## 4 DALANG II/III (TYPE 922III/IIIA) CLASS (SUBMARINE SUPPORT SHIPS) (ASL)

- Bei Ju 138

- Dong Ju 332

- Nan Ju 501

Displacement, tonnes: 3,700 standard; 4,200 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet): 111.9 × 14.6 × 4.3 (367.1 × 47.9 × 14.1)

Speed, knots: 16

Range, n miles: 8,000 at 14 kt

Complement: 180

Machinery: 2 diesels; 4,000 hp(m) (2.94 MW); 2 shafts Guns: 4 Type 61/76 37 mm (2 twin) (122 [Dalang II]).

Radars: Navigation: Fin Curve; I-band

Comment: Construction of the first Type 922ll class (305 [ex-Nan Ju 503]) began at Guangzhou Shipyard in September 1971. It was commissioned in November 1975 and later transferred to the fisheries agency in 2006 and subsequently to the Coast Guard (Haijing 3411) in 2013. As a result of experience gained, development of an improved Type 922lll (Dalang II) version began in 1978. Construction of the first of these ships (Bei Ju 122) began in December 1982 at Wuchang Shipyard, Wuhan, and the ship later commissioned in 1986. Subsequently, three further modified Type 922lllA (Dalang III) were built: Dong Ju 332 (1999), Bei Ju 138 (1992) and Nan Ju 501 (1995). These modifications include changes to upper deck design and the possible incorporation of a decompression chamber. Basing: 122 and 138 in North Sea Fleet; 332 in East Sea Fleet and 501 in South Sea Fleet. 501 was responsible for taking an umanned underwater vehicle from the sea in December 2016 when USNS Bowditch was attempting to recover it. attempting to recover it.

## 1 DONGHAI DAO (MODIFIED HANSA SONDERBURG) CLASS

(AK)

Builders Wenchong Shipyard, Guangzhou DONGHAI DAO 10 Jul 2015

Displacement, tonnes: 20,000 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $175.5 \times 32.4 \times ?$  (575.8 × 106.3 × ?)

Speed, knots: 14

Machinery: To be announced Radars: To be announced.

Comment: A semi-submersible transport ship was commissioned into the South Sea Fleet in July 2015. The ship is superficially similar to but smaller than the US Navy's 240 m Expeditionary Transport Dock ships. The principal design feature is a cut-down submersible hull section with a crane at each end. The principal roles of the ship include transport of heavy equipment and small craft; it has been observed carrying a Zubr-class air-cushioned vehicle. It was also used to transport equipment required to set up the PLA Navy's first overseas logistics facility in Djibouti in August 2017. The ship could also be used as a forward operating base and/or repair centre.

## 4 DACHOU (TYPE 917A) CLASS (AGT)

- Nan Yun 846

- Nan Yun 847

Radars: To be announced.

Comment: Torpedo recovery vessels, which appear similar in design to that of the Wochi-class mine countermeasures vessels. The first was built at Wuzhou Shipyard and entered service in 2006. Constructed with a hydraulically operated stern ramp to facilitate torpedo recovery. Single hydraulic crane on quarterdeck for recovering torpedoes from abeam or astern. Basing: 530 in the North Sea Fleet, 760 in the East Sea Fleet, and 846 and 847 in the South Sea Fleet.

## **ICEBREAKERS**

Notes: The Polar Research Institute operates the icebreaker Xuelong (Snow Dragon) (1993, 15,352 gt). Construction of a second ship, *Xuelong 2* (13,996 tonnes), commenced at Jiangnan Shipyard in 2016. Entered service by July 2019.

## 2 YANRAO (TYPE 272) CLASS (ICEBREAKERS) (AGBH)

Builders Laid down Liaonan Shipyard, Lushun Nov 2013 Commissioned Mar 2015 28 Dec 2015 Yan Bing 723 Liaonan Shipyard, Lushun Jul 2015

Displacement, tonnes: 4,860 full load

Dimensions, metres (feet): 103.1 × 18.4 × ? (338.3 × 60.4 × ?)

Speed, knots: 18 Complement: 90

Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts Radars: Navigation: 2 I-band. Helicopters: Platform for 1 Z-8.

Comment: A class of icebreaker designed to operate primarily in the Bohai Sea. Capable of breaking ice 1 m thick. The vessels are larger than the preceding Yanha class and design features include a helicopter deck aft, but no hangar. Based in North Sea Fleet.

## **TUGS**

Notes: There are several classes of harbour tugs of the order of 30 m length. These include: Duda class (Bei Tuo 632, 681, 685, 769 [North], Dong Tuo 874, 876, 878, 879 [East], Nan Tuo 172, 176, 177 [South]); Duhast class (Bei Tuo 633, 719, 720, 725, 733 [North], Dong Tuo 832, 876, 880 [East], Nan Tuo 180–183, 186, 187 [South]); Ducha class (Bei Tuo 624–627, 629, 715, 718 [North], Dong Tuo 871–873 [East], Nan Tuo 169–170, 173, 178, 179 [South]). There are also more than 15 new Dupo class, including Nan Tuo 192 in the South.

## ARMY

Notes: (1) The army operates armed patrol craft, as well as watercraft and ships for transport and logistic tasks, however, also noted to take part in amphibious assault exercises with the navy. Distinguished by blue-grey colour scheme and markings, including pennant numbers prefixed by two letters to denote district or region assigned, for example ND, LD, BD. (2) Craft include Type 271 LCUs, Type 068/059 LCMs, and LCVPs.

## 3 TYPE 701 CLASS (LOGISTIC SUPPORT SHIP) (AKLRH)

GY 820

Displacement, tonnes: 3,500 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $90 \times 14.6 \times ?$  (295.3 × 47.9 × ?) Speed, knots: 20 Range, n miles: 3,000 at 12 kt Machinery: CODAD; 4 diesels; 2 shafts; bow thruster Guns: 4 H/PJ-15 30 mm or 8—14.5 mm MGs (4 twin).

Helicopters: Platform only for a Z-9.

Comment: Class of logistic support ships completed at Songliao Shipyard in 2013-18. Landing ship design, which features bow and stern ramps and internal cargo deck. The ship can transport large equipment and is mainly used for material supply, equipment transportation, and maritime rescue missions. GY 820 began its service in Sansha City (Heinan province). The vessel serves under the Guangzhou Military Command. Its primary function is to resupply the homeport at Sansha on Yongxing Island, the largest in the Paracel group seized by China following a brief war with South Vietnam in 1974.

## AIR FORCE

**Notes:** The air force operates armed patrol craft, as well as watercraft and ships for transport and logistic tasks. Distinguished by dark grey colour scheme and markings, including pennant numbers prefixed by K, for example KZ and KT.

## **GOVERNMENT MARITIME FORCES**

Notes: Chinese government maritime forces have undergone a series of organisational changes since 2000. The first step was to transform a variety of maritime militias, managed changes since 2000. The first step was to transform a variety of martine militials, managed on a regional basis, to nationally funded, owned, and operated maritime forces. By 2010, the five principal organisations had become: The China Marine Surveillance (CMS) force of the State Oceanic Administration, the Fisheries Law Enforcement Command (FLEC) of the Fisheries Bureau, the Maritime Safety Administration of the Ministry of Transport, the China Coast Guard (Maritime Police) of the People's Armed Police Force, and the Customs force of the General Administration of Customs, China announced on 10 March 2013 that all the law the General Administration of Customs. China announced on 10 March 2013 that all the law enforcement forces (Coast Guard, CMS, FLEC, and Customs) would be amalgamated under the State Oceanic Administration, administered by the Ministry of Land and Resources under a new force known as the China Coast Guard. On 1 July 2018 the China Coast Guard was transferred from the State Council and the State Oceanic Administration (civilian) to the Chinese People's Armed Police force, placing it under the command of the Central Military Commission again. The Maritime Safety Administration remains a separate organisation accountable to the Ministry of Transport for maritime safety and counter-pollution issues. There also appears to be a cadre of 'maritime militia', typically disguised as fishermen, which act as irregular government forces in support of maritime claims. Little is known about the organisation but members seen to have received military training and sometimes wear uniform.

#### MARITIME RESCUE, SAFETY AND LOGISTIC SUPPORT

Notes: (1) The Maritime Safety Administration (MSA) belongs to the Ministry of Transport. MSA is responsible for the policy for and supervision of water safety and marine pollution prevention; safety and certification of Chinese flagged ships and foreign ships entering Chinese waters; qualifications and management of seafarers; navigational safety and aids to navigation and marine search and rescue. The agency is organised into 14 Regional MSAs along the coastline and Yangtze, Pearl, and Heilongjiang rivers. The patrol force includes some 1,300 vessels (of which some 200 are more than 20 m long).

(2) In addition to the vessels listed, ships in excess of 60 m length include: Haixun 103 (95 m Shugong class).

(3) There are number of patrol boats of about 45 m, including Haixun 0613 (ex-091) (46 m), Haixun 0639 (46.5 m), Haixun 0717 (47 m), Haixun 0801 (46 m), and Haixun 1011 (49 m). Construction of five 45 m units started at Guangzhou Huangpu Shipyard in August 2019. (4) There is a large fleet of Type 30 m patrol boats for SAR tasks, plus a riverine variant. (5) There is at least one oil recovery ship, Haixun 0512 (ex-Haite 071) of about 60 m delivered in April 2012.

Comment: Group of patrol ships classed as Type 60 m and two main sub types. Type A built about 2005–10, and Type B 2009–20. Roles include patrol, search-and-rescue, and pollution prevention. Built by about nine shipyards (Huanghai Shipbuilding, Huangpu Shipyard, Huangpu Wenchong, Guijiang Shipbuilding, Tongfang Jiangxin Shipbuilding, Weihai Donghai Shipbuilding, Wuchang Heavy Industries, Wuhan Nanhua Fast Ship Engineering, Xijiang Shipyard) and the total number of ships is unknown. There are differences between reported ships, including several propulsion configurations and variants with and without flight decks. Details reflect Type B, with Type A smaller at about 61.2 m length and 9 m beam. Twin shaft propulsion for speeds of 16–21.5 kt, and several with three engines capable of 23+ kt. Type B ships are noted to be ice-strengthened.

#### 1 SHENHAI 01 CLASS (WSAR)

Launched Huangpu Wenchong Shipbuilding SHENHAI 01 28 Apr 2020 Aug 2020

Displacement, tonnes: 1,450 full load Dimensions, metres (feet):  $78\times12.8\times3.4$  (255.9  $\times$  42.0  $\times$  11.2)

Speed, knots: 18 Complement: 60

Machinery: Diesel-electric hybrid; 3 diesel generators; 8,484 hp (6.24 MW); lithium-ion batteries; 2 ABB Azipod azimuth thrusters; 8,158 hp (6 MW); bow thruster

Radars: Surface search/navigation: 1 E/F-band. Navigation: 2 I-band.

Comment: Reported as first Chinese-built hybrid diesel-electric emergency rescue vessel for maritime law enforcement, search and rescue (SAR), and pollution monitoring. Launched by Huangpu Wenchong Shipbuilding in April 2020 and delivered to Shenzhen Maritime Safety Administration (MSA) on 18 August 2020. Hybrid propulsion system by ABB, including lithium-ion battery sets with 1,880 kWh total capacity and full electric propulsion mode. Other features include flight deck, LNG gas detection system, ship air pollution emission detection system, oil spill monitoring radar, and ROVs.

#### **COAST GUARD**

Notes: (1) The China Coast Guard (CCG) was formerly the maritime branch of the Public Security Border Troops, a paramilitary police force under the leadership of the Ministry of Public Security (MPS). It was announced on 10 March 2013 that this force was to be amalgamated with the forces of the China Marine Surveillance (CMS), the Fisheries Law Enforcement Command (FLEC), and Customs to form a new CCG force commanded by the State Oceanic Administration, an arm of the Ministry of Land and Resources. On 1 July 2018 the China Coast Guard was transferred from the State Council and the State Oceanic Administration (civilian) to the Chinese People's Armed Police force, placing it under the command of the Central Military Commission. All CCG ship numbers are prefixed 'Haijing' and these now also include ex-CMS ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Yuzheng' and ex-Customs ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', ex-FLEC ships, formerly prefixed 'Haijian', e

ships, formerly prefixed 'Haiguan'.

(2) Ships feature white hulls and superstructure with diagonal red, blue, and white stripes and China Coast Guard markings. A new numbering system started to be applied to pennant numbers in 2019, comprised of either four digits (ships reporting a district command) or five digits (reporting to regional detachment). With a few exceptions, the numbers listed reflect the previously reported system.

previously reported system.

(3) The six districts are prefixed by the number 1 (Shanghai), 2 (Ningbo), 3 (Guangzhou), 4 (Wenchang), 5 (Sanya), and 6 (Qingdao) and the second digit indicates tonnage.

(4) The regional detachments are prefixed by the number 11 (Jiangsu), 12 (Shanghai), 13 (Zhejiang), 14 (Fujian), 21 (Guangcang), 22 (Guangxi), 23 (Hainan), 31 (Liaoning), 32 (Hebei), 33 (Tianjin), and 34 (Shandong). The third digit may still indicate tonnage.

(5) There are more than 100 20 m Shaokao-class patrol craft, which have both Haijing and Haijian pennant numbers, and the Hongshou-class patrol craft of 42 m.

(6) There are two patrol ships of about 57 m, Yuzheng 21001 and Yuzheng 21103.

(7) The Kaobo class are auxiliairies of about 50 m. There is also a 90 m Yunsong-class auxiliary.

(8) The Coast Guard operates helicooters, including the Z-9 type.

(8) The Coast Guard operates helicopters, including the Z-9 type.

|   | - (ex-Baoding)        | 1108<br>(ex-511)  | Wuchang Shipyard,<br>Wuhan               | 2014              | 22 Oct 2015             | 12 Dec 2016                 |
|   | - (ex-Ningde)         | - (ex-510)        | Huangpu Shipyard,<br>Guangzhou           | 2014              | 24 Oct 2015             | 28 Dec 2016                 |

Displacement, tonnes: 1,300 standard

Dimensions, metres (feet):  $89.0 \times 11.1 \times 4.4$  ( $292.0 \times 36.4 \times 14.4$ )

Speed, knots: 25 Range, n miles: 3,500 at 16 kt Complement: 60 (18 officers)

Machinery: 2 diesels; 2 shafts; cp props
Guns: 1 H/PJ-26 76 mm/59 (AK-176); 120 rds/min to 15 km (8.1 n miles); weight of shell 5.9 kg.
2 H/PJ-15 30 mm (Type 056 ships) or H/PJ-17 30 mm (Type 056A); 350 rds/min to 3 km
(1.6 n miles). 2—12.7 mm or 14.5 mm machine guns.
Physical countermeasures: Decoys: 2 9-barrelled launchers.

Electronic countermeasures: ESM: To be announced. Radars: Air/surface search: Type 364 (Seagull C 5); G/H/I/J-bands. Surface search: I-band.

Navigation: 2 Kaige; I-band. Fire control: H/LJP-349A; I-band. Sonars: Bow-mounted sonar.

Combat data systems: ZKJ-5 II Combat Command System. Satcom. Electro-optic systems: IR-17 optronic sensor. Helicopters: Platform for 1 Z-9C/D.

Programmes: Converted corvettes. Indications of a new corvette design for the PLAN emerged in November 2010. The design was broadly based on the Pattani class built for Thailand in 2005–06. Series production at four shipyards delivered 22 Type 056 and 40 Type 056A hulls. In late 2021 it was reported that all earlier Jiangdao (Type 056) units not equipped with a VDS would be transferred to the Coast Guard. The modifications under way, as seen on hull number 511, include the removal of missile (VJ-83, anti-ship and Hongqi-10, air defence) and torpedo launchers. LED panels to display messages added to the port and starboard sides of torpeo launchers. LED pariets to display inessages added to the plot and standard sides of the superstructure as well as water cannons. Specifications are based on vessels operated by the PLAN and may be different. 582, 596, 584, 583, 587, 586, 503, and 511 were already reported to be decommissioned by the PLAN in November 2021. 509 was reported to be decommissioned in December, 588 and 512 in January 2022, 589 and 595 in March 2022, and 510 and 592 in May 2022. All 22 Type 056 converted to Coast Guard vessels by January 2023.

# Colombia

# ARMADA DE LA REPUBLICA

#### Country overview

The Republic of Colombia is the only South American country that fronts both the Caribbean Sea and the Pacific Ocean with coastlines of 950 n miles and 782 n miles respectively. With an area of 440,831 square miles, it is bordered to the north by Panama, to the east by Venezuela and Brazil, and to the south by Peru and Ecuador. The capital and largest city is Bogotá. Buenaventura and Tumaco are the main Pacific ports while Cartagena, Santa Marta, and Barranquilla, which is near the mouth of the principal river and transport artery, the Magdalena, are on the Caribbean side. Territorial seas (12 n miles) are claimed a 20n o mile exclusive miles) are claimed but while it has claimed a 200 n mile exclusive economic zone (EEZ), its limits have not been fully defined.

#### Headquarters appointments

Commander of the Navy: Vice Admiral Francisco Hernando Cubides Granados Deputy Commander and Chief of Staff of the Navy: Vice Admiral Juan Ricardo Rozo Obregón

Chief of Naval Operations Vice Admiral Orlando Enrique Grisales Franceschi Commander Caribbean Force

Rear Admiral Hernando Enrique Mattos Dager Commander Pacific Force: Rear Admiral Carlos Alberto Serrano Guzmán

Vice Admiral Harry Ernesto Reyno Nino Commander Marine Corps: Brigadier General I M Jorge Federico Torres Mora

- 2020: 33,824 (including 23,456 marines, 200 coastguards, and 150 naval aviators)
- 6,500 reserve 2 years' national service

## Organisation

Caribbean Force Command: HQ at Cartagena. Pacific Force Command: HQ at Bahia Malaga. Eastern Force Command: HQ at Puerto Carreño Naval Force South: HQ at Puerto Leguízamo. Riverine Brigade: HQ at Bogotá, DC. Coast Guard: HQ at Bogotá.

ARC Bolivar, Cartagena, Main naval base (floating dock, 1 slipway), schools. ARC Bahía Málaga: Major Pacific base. ARC Barranquilla: Naval training base. ARC Puerto Leguizamo: Putumayo River base. Turbo: Minor River base. Puerto López: Minor River base. Puerto Carreño: Minor River base. Inrida: Minor River base. San Andrés y Providencia: Specific Command

## Aviation

Baranquilla: new base opened in September 2009.

Forces Command.

The Marine Corps has its headquarters (HQ) in Bogotá. It consists of five brigades as follows: Marine Infantry Brigade No 1 (BRIM1) (Corozal).
Marine Infantry Brigade No 2 (BRIM2) (Bahia Malaga).
Marine Infantry Brigade No 3 (BRIM3) (Puerto Leguizamo).

#### Prefix to ships' names

ARC (Armada Republica de Colombia)

#### Dimar

Maritime authority in charge of hydrography and navigational

#### Coast Guard and Customs (DIAN)

The Coast Guard was established in 1979 but then gave way to the Customs Service before being re-established in January 1992 under the control of the Navy. Headquarters at Bogotá. Main bases are Cartagena, Buenaventura y Turbo and Valle. Ships have a red and yellow diagonal stripe on the hull and patrol craft have a PM number. Customs craft were absorbed into the Coast Guard but by 1995 were again independent as part of the DIAN (Direccion de Impuestos y Aduanas Nacionales). Customs craft have Aduana written on the ship's side, a thick and two this diagonal stripes and have Alvan and two thin diagonal stripes and have AN numbers.
